<script type="text/javascript">

if(typeof(vo)=="undefined"){
    if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"initializing vo"});}
    voCatcher = false;
    vo = new Object({
        embed:[],
        embedPost:[],
        standalone:[]
    });
    function tncms_video_ad(adId, videoUrl, videoClickUri, properties){
        if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"catching video ad: " + adId});}
        
        videoUrlPath = window.location.protocol+"//"+window.location.host

        
        if(properties.embed==1){
            if(properties.rolltype=="post"){
            vo.embedPost.push({
                adId:adId,
                videoUrl:videoUrlPath+videoUrl,
                videoClickUri:videoClickUri,
                width:properties.width,
                height:properties.height,
                volume:properties.volume,
                autoplay:properties.autoplay,
                rolltype:properties.rolltype,
                playlistItem:{


    url:window.location.protocol+"//"+window.location.host+videoUrl,
    autoPlay:true,
    autoBuffering:false,
    onStart: function(){ if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Start Event: "+clip.url});}
        if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Playing: "+clip.url});}
        if(typeof(_gaq)!="undefined"){
            var clipType = clip.url.split(".")[clip.url.split(".").length-1];
                
            if(clipType!="jpg"){
                if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Playing: "+clip.url+" type: "+clipType});}
                _gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'videos', 'play', clip.url]);
            }
        }else{if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Playing: "+clip.url+" _gaq undefined"});}}        
    },
    
    onResume: function(clip) {  
        if(typeof(_gaq)!="undefined"){
            var clipType = clip.url.split(".")[clip.url.split(".").length-1];             
            if(clipType!="jpg"){
                if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Resuming: "+clip.url});}
                _gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'videos', 'play', clip.url]);
            }
        }else{if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Resuming: "+clip.url+" _gaq undefined"});}}      
    },

    onPause: function(clip) {
        if(typeof(_gaq)!="undefined"){
            var clipType = clip.url.split(".")[clip.url.split(".").length-1];
                
            if(clipType!="jpg"){
                if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Paused: "+clip.url});}
                _gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'videos', 'pause', clip.url, parse(this.getTime())]);
            }
        }else{if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Paused: "+clip.url+" _gaq undefined"});}}
    },

    onStop: function(clip) {
        if(typeof(_gaq)!="undefined"){
            var clipType = clip.url.split(".")[clip.url.split(".").length-1];
                
            if(clipType!="jpg"){
                if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Stopped: "+clip.url});}
                _gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'videos', 'stop', clip.url, parseInt(this.getTime())]);
            }
        }else{if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Stopped: "+clip.url+" _gaq undefined"});}}    
    },

    onFinish: function(clip) {
        if(typeof(_gaq)!="undefined"){
            var clipType = clip.url.split(".")[clip.url.split(".").length-1];
                
            if(clipType!="jpg"){
                if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Finished: "+clip.url});}
                _gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'videos', 'finish', clip.url]);
            }
        }else{if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"Video Ad - Finished: "+clip.url+" _gaq undefined"});}}
    },
    onBeforeFinish: function(){
        vo.post[0].watched = true;
        vo.post[0].lock = false;

            if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"finished playing ad video"});}
            
        
        if(automaticSwapFromAd){
            
            if(typeof(ninjaLog)!="undefined"){ninjaLog.Update({text:"attempting to swap to active video in to "+this.id()});}
            swapSubstituteHTML("#"+this.id(),jQuery("#"+this.id()).parents(".blox-multimedia").find(".blox-multimedia-text .item.playing a.load-video").first());

        }

        automaticSwapFromAd = false;
        vo.post.reverse().pop();
        
    }


},
                properties:properties
            });
            }else{
            vo.embed.push({
                adId:adId,
                videoUrl:videoUrlPath+videoUrl,
                videoClickUri:videoClickUri,
                width:properties.width,
                height:properties.height,
                volume:properties.volume,
                autoplay:properties.autoplay,

	<script type="text/javascript">
	// <![CDATA[
		$(function(){
			var $popover = $.Deferred()
				.done(function(){
					var $i = $('#popoverAd');
						$i.find('.tncms-region-ads').show();
						$i.css({
							left:$(window).width()/2 - ($i.width()/2),
							top:($(window).height()/2) - ($i.height()/2)
						}).show();
						$i.siblings('.ui-widget-overlay').css({
							width: $(window).width(),
							height: $(document).height()
						}).show();
						$i.find('.close').bind('click',function(){
							$i.siblings('.ui-widget-overlay').fadeOut(750).
							siblings('#popoverAd').animate({left:-$i.outerWidth()}, 750, 'easeInOutBack');
						});
				});

			// logic for whether to load popover or not
			var bloxAdpopover = $.cookie('blox-popover');
			// No longer creating EMPTY cookie, so the ad can be section specific.
                        //if (bloxAdpopover != 'EMPTY'){
				if( $('#popoverAd .tncms-region-ads').children(':not("script")').length==0 ){

// login display based on cookie
    var sUsername = $.cookie('tncms-screenname');

    if(sUsername != null){insertableUserName=", <a href=\"/users/profile/"+sUsername.replace(/\+/g," ")+"\">"+sDisplayname.replace(/\+/g,"&nbsp;")+"</a>";}
    var welcomeMessage = "Welcome back"+insertableUserName;    

    if ((sAuthToken == null) ) {
        $('#post-comment').hide();
        $('#logout-dialog').hide();
        $('.uNavOut').hide();
        $('.uNavReauth').remove();
        $('.not-logged-in').show();

    } else {
        if(typeof(loggedInText)!="undefined"){if(loggedInText!=""){
            welcomeMessage = loggedInText.replace("[USER_NAME]",insertableUserName);
        }}
        $('#login-dialog').hide();
        $('.uUser').html(welcomeMessage);
        $('.uNav').hide();
        $('.uNavOut').show();
        $('.uNavReauth').hide();

        $('#post-comment').show();
        $('.not-logged-in').hide();
        $('.logged-in').show();

        if($('#customAvatar').length > 0){
            $('#defaultAvatar').hide();
            $('#customAvatar').show();
        }else{           
            $('#defaultAvatar').remove();
            $('.uIcon').each(function(index) { 
                if ($(this).children().length==0){
                    $(this).append('<img class="custom-avatar" src="'+sAvatar+'" alt="custom avatar"/>');
                }
            });    
        }
    }
    // show panel when user info is in place
    $('div.blox-user-panel dl').show();

	function savelogoutParams() {		
		var cur_params = window.location.href.match(/\?.*/);
		if (cur_params){
			cur_params = cur_params.toString();
			var orig_refer = $(".logout-form").find('input[name="referer_url"]').val();
			if (orig_refer) orig_refer = orig_refer.toString();
			var cur_paramsString = cur_params.replace(/[\?&]_dc=[0-9.]*/,"");
			if (orig_refer.indexOf("?") != -1){
				cur_paramsString = cur_paramsString.replace("?","&");
			}
			if (cur_paramsString){
				var final_refer = orig_refer+cur_paramsString; 
				$(".logout-form").find('input[name="referer_url"]').val(final_refer);
				var test_val = $(".logout-form").find('input[name="referer_url"]').val();
			}
		}	
	}

	<script type="text/javascript">
		

		

		

		


		
		
		
		
		
		
		
		

		
			$(".mega-nav-container").each(function() {

			
				var bLeftSideEmpty = "true";
				$(".nav-content-left .tncms-region", this).each(function() {
					if($(this).html() != '') {
						bLeftSideEmpty = "false";
					}
				});
				if(bLeftSideEmpty == "true"){$(".nav-content-left", this).addClass("hide");}
				
				var bRightSideEmpty = "true";
				$(".nav-content-right .tncms-region", this).each(function() {
					if($(this).html() != '') {
						bRightSideEmpty = "false";
					}
				});
				if(bRightSideEmpty == "true"){$(".nav-content-right", this).addClass("hide");}
				if(bLeftSideEmpty == "true" && bRightSideEmpty == "true") {
					$(this).addClass("unmega");
					var unmegaPosition = $(this).parent().position();
					if(unmegaPosition.left + 160 > 960) {
						$(this).css('right', '0px');
					}
				}
				if((bLeftSideEmpty == "true" && bRightSideEmpty == "false") || (bLeftSideEmpty == "false" && bRightSideEmpty == "true")){
					$(this).addClass("onemega");
					var onemegaPosition = $(this).parent().position();
					if(onemegaPosition.left + 550 > 960) {
						$(this).css('right', '0px');
					}
				}
			});
			
		
		
	</script>

							<div class="panel-content-container" class="blox-transparency">
								<h3><a href="/arts_and_entertainment/the-vmas-what-worked-what-didn-t-what-was-miley/article_e08f0b5c-0e80-11e3-b47e-001a4bcf6878.html">The VMAs: What worked, what didn't, what was Miley Cyrus</a></h3>
								
								
								<div class="panel-content">
									<p class="byline">Christopher James, A&E Editor</p>
									
										<div class="panel-leadin">
											The MTV Video Music Awards (VMAs) have long been one of the craziest and most unpredictable nights of televised award shows. From the Madonna-Brittney Spears liplock to Kanye West stealing the microphone from Taylor Swift, it's guaranteed that at least one huge music artist will behave insanely. (We're looking at you, Miley Cyrus.) 
										</div>

							<div class="panel-content-container" class="blox-transparency">
								<h3><a href="/arts_and_entertainment/film_tv/student-to-screen-film-at-cannes-film-festival/article_a8a3c8e4-b210-11e2-97c7-001a4bcf6878.html">Student to screen film at Cannes Film Festival</a></h3>
								
								
								<div class="panel-content">
									<p class="byline">By Mary Carreon
A&E Intern</p>
									
										<div class="panel-leadin">
											From athletes to artists, LMU has an incredibly talented student body. Last week, senior film production major Alex Michael Harris was chosen to have his film screened at the Cannes Film Festival in France. The goal of the prestigious film festival is to aid the development of cinema, boost the film industry and celebrate cinema at the international level. Over the weekend, the Loyolan sat down with Harris to chat with him about his film, “Perfect Jimmy,” and the festival screening.

		<script type="text/javascript">
			var sliderPresentationId = "#slideshow-presentation-1";
			$(document).ready(function() {
				var sliderPresentationId = "#slideshow-presentation-1";
				$(sliderPresentationId + " .slideshow-presentation-nav-item a").click(function(event) {
					event.preventDefault();
				});

			/* rotation function */
				var changePanelTimeout;
				var currIndex = -1;
				var currPanel;
				var currNav;
				var newIndex;
				var newPanel;
				var totalPanels;
				var newIndex = -1;
				
				function changePanel(newIndex){
					clearTimeout(changePanelTimeout);
					var currPanel = $(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-panel-item.active-panel");
					var currNav = $(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item.active-nav");
					if(typeof newIndex == "undefined") {
						if(currPanel.next().length == 0) {
							currPanel.clearQueue().fadeTo(100,0).removeClass("active-panel");
							currNav.removeClass("active-nav");
							currPanel.css("display", "none");
							$(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item").eq(0).addClass("active-nav");
							$(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-panel-item").eq(0).clearQueue().fadeTo(100,1).addClass("active-panel");
						} else { 
							currNav.removeClass("active-nav");
							currPanel.clearQueue().fadeTo(100,0).removeClass("active-panel");
							currPanel.css("display", "none");
							currPanel.clearQueue().next().fadeTo(100,1).addClass("active-panel");
							currNav.next().addClass("active-nav");
						}
					} else { 
							currNav.removeClass("active-nav");
							currPanel.clearQueue().fadeTo(100,0).removeClass("active-panel");
							currPanel.css("display", "none");
							$(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-panel-item").eq(newIndex).clearQueue().fadeTo(100,1).addClass("active-panel");
							$(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item").eq(newIndex).addClass("active-nav");
					}
					changePanelTimeout = setTimeout(changePanel,5000);     
				}

				changePanel(0);
							
			/* Stop rotation on panel hover */
				$(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-panel-item").hover(
				function() {
						clearTimeout(changePanelTimeout);
					},
					function() {
						changePanelTimeout = setTimeout(changePanel,5000);
					});

			/* Navigation item behavior */
				
					$(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item").click(function() {
						changePanel($(sliderPresentationId + " li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item").index(this));
					});
				
				
				
			});

			/* Set first and last navigation items, and fade in first panel */
				/* $(sliderPresentationId + ' li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item').eq(0).addClass("first-in-list");
				$(sliderPresentationId + ' li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item').eq(($(sliderPresentationId + ' li.slideshow-presentation-nav-item').length)-1).addClass("last-in-list"); */
			
			
		</script>

                            Author talks queer culture on campus
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/author-talks-queer-culture-on-campus/article_c84be866-a487-11e2-88d7-001a4bcf6878.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="2 images">

                            <p><p>“Just so you know, I welcome whatever sort of controversy, questions, discussions … glamour … that may come up.” So author Mattilda Bernstein Sycamore begins her talk with a group of communication studies students and professors last Thursday. As part of the School of Communication and Fine Arts’ Visiting Artists &amp; Lecture Series, Sycamore came to speak about her book, titled “The End of San Francisco,” and the questions it raises about the realities of searching for and uniting a queer culture community.</p></p>

                            <p><p>With the 2012 presidential election looming, the political landscape is filled with debates over issues such as abortion and women’s rights. In order to help engender discussion on this issue, the William H. Hannon Library will be holding a Faculty Pub Night with LMU philosophy professor Dr. Christopher Kaczor regarding his latest book, “The Ethics of Abortion: Women’s Rights, Human Life, and the Question of Justice.”</p></p>

                            ‘Swirling’ authors share interracial dating insights 
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            Tyler Barnett
A&E Intern

                            <p><p>Chocolate or Vanilla? Some people prefer chocolate and some prefer vanilla but some prefer to swirl. The image of a swirled ice cream cone is the graphic that graces the cover of the book “Swirling: How to Date, Mate and Relate. Mixing Race, Culture, and Creed.”</p></p>

         <div class="day-partition">Thursday 10/04/2012</div>
           
            

            <dl class="grid_  even-list-item">
    <dt class="bucket-photo">
                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/students-gather-to-read-and-take-pictures-with-banned-books/article_e41930da-0d10-11e2-bd56-001a4bcf6878.html" title="Students gather to read and take pictures with banned books">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/f/40/f4031672-0d11-11e2-ae91-001a4bcf6878/506bbdca962f9.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/students-gather-to-read-and-take-pictures-with-banned-books/article_e41930da-0d10-11e2-bd56-001a4bcf6878.html" title="Students gather to read and take pictures with banned books">
                            Students gather to read and take pictures with banned books
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/students-gather-to-read-and-take-pictures-with-banned-books/article_e41930da-0d10-11e2-bd56-001a4bcf6878.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="3 images">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            Christopher James
A&E Editor
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Posted: October 04, 2012
    </em></dd>
                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>What do “The Hunger Games” and “The Catcher in the Rye” have in common? Besides centering on troubled young adults in a harsh world, they are also two of many classic or popular novels that are banned or have had their content seriously challenged. During Convo this past Tuesday, Oct. 2, the William H. Hannon Library set up a table out in front of the Lair Marketplace filled with some of the most popular and classic books which just happen to be banned by some sectors of the U.S. Students were invited to take their pictures with the banned books of their choice, and one person was selected to win a free T-shirt to commemorate Banned Book Week. When asked his favorite banned book, mechanical engineering graduate student Rendle Myles (pictured below) said, “I chose ‘The Color Purple’ because of how it dealt with the racism against blacks in the 1960s.” Sophomore film production major Ashley Wilson found the event to be important and informative. “Not a lot of people know [these books] are banned. People come up and are surprised ‘The Hunger Games’ is banned. People know these books are cherished,” Wilson said While many of the students who attended the event grabbed “The Hunger Games” to take pictures with, other students had unique tastes in banned books. Sophomore marketing and English double major Jenny Yu, a copy editor at the Loyolan, picked “East of Eden” as her banned book to take a picture with. “That book is so enlightening about so many issues. Steinback is the bomb,” she said. Whatever one’s taste is, it seems that most people have at least once cherished book that is banned in certain communities.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/wrongfully-imprisoned-man-shares-stories-from-death-row/article_2d8c3994-0a85-11e2-8e6f-0019bb30f31a.html" title="Wrongfully imprisoned man shares stories from death row">
                            Wrongfully imprisoned man shares stories from death row
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/wrongfully-imprisoned-man-shares-stories-from-death-row/article_2d8c3994-0a85-11e2-8e6f-0019bb30f31a.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            Christopher James
A&E Editor
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Posted: October 01, 2012
    </em></dd>
                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Fate just seems to keep bringing me back to the West Memphis Three. On Wednesday, Sept. 27, I drove down to UCLA to attend a Q&amp;A with one of the members of the West Memphis Three, Damien Echols, about his new memoir “Life After Death.” I had rushed to the UCLA Freud Playhouse right at the stroke of 7 p.m. only to realize I had forgotten the receipt to pick up my ticket. All of a sudden, a random passerby slammed a ticket down on the table next to me and said, “Take it, man, it’s free.”</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/faculty-pub-night-tackles-faith-and-politics/article_671e4c6c-ff84-11e1-8d66-001a4bcf6878.html" title="Faculty Pub Night tackles faith and politics">
                            Faculty Pub Night tackles faith and politics
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            Christopher James, Asst. A&E Editor

    <em class="item-updated">
        Posted: September 17, 2012

            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Separation of church and state is one of the essential foundations our country was built on. However, with another election coming up, we see time and time again how the two intermingle as party lines and ways of thinking and voting stem from religious beliefs.</p></p>

                            <p><p>“The book that you hold in your hands is revolutionary.” So begins the forward to Canadian minister Brian Arthur Brown’s new book “Three Testaments: Torah, Gospel, and Quran.”</p></p>

                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/author-reminisces-on-college-career/article_165f3d06-fc94-11e1-b695-001a4bcf6878.html" title="Author reminisces on college career">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/9/c6/9c62e4de-fc94-11e1-b26e-001a4bcf6878/505013db37ada.preview-100.jpg" />

                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/author-reminisces-on-college-career/article_165f3d06-fc94-11e1-b695-001a4bcf6878.html" title="Author reminisces on college career">
                            Author reminisces on college career
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/author-reminisces-on-college-career/article_165f3d06-fc94-11e1-b695-001a4bcf6878.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            James Meador 
Courtesy of Picador 
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Posted: September 13, 2012
    </em></dd>
                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Running into prestigious, famous and award-winning artists is a treat that students can partake in being at a Los Angeles-based school. All it takes is scrolling through the local Barnes and Noble calendar to catch a particularly interesting Q&amp;A with an author. The Loyolan was contacted by Picador, the publishing company behind Pulitzer Prize-winning author Jeffrey Eugenides’ work, about publishing an interview with the author. Having written “The Virgin Suicides,” “Middlesex” and “The Marriage Plot,” Eugenides certainly knows how to get inside the psyche of a young adult audience. His college career was a time in his life that was of particular interest to him, and he has done interviews specifically geared towards college audience. The following is an interview done with Eugenides by James Meador of Picador publishing company.</p></p>

            </dd>

                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/alumna-to-discuss-her-novel/article_8d61b81e-75ff-11e1-ba64-0019bb30f31a.html" title="Alumna to discuss her novel">
                            Alumna to discuss her novel
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/alumna-to-discuss-her-novel/article_8d61b81e-75ff-11e1-ba64-0019bb30f31a.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>

                        <p class="byline">
                            Raeesah Reese, Staff Writer

    <em class="item-updated">

                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p><span>As </span>an alumna as well as Professor Emerita here at LMU, Dr. Graciela Limón will be sharing her considerable experience with writing at an event at William H. Hannon Library. She will be the latest guest speaker for the library’s Alumni Authors series on Wednesday, March 28 at 6 p.m. The event, which is sponsored by the Department of Chicana/o Studies and Sigma Lambda Gamma, “is going to be a unique opportunity to see a world class author speak about her life and writing,” said Jaime Hazlitt, the outreach librarian for the event. </p></p>

                            Jewish Sunday Book Group covers experimental novel 'Bernhard'
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            Daniel Steingold
                        </p>

                            <p><p>On Sunday Feb. 12, LMU's own Jewish Studies Sunday Book &amp;
Discussion Group will be holding a discussion on "Bernhard," a
novel by Yoel Hoffmann. One of many such events, the goal of the
club is to both promote the university's Jewish Studies program and
to increase attendance to campus activities. Both LMU students and
the local community are welcome to attend.</p></p>

                            <p><p>Have you ever wondered what it would be like to be an author
with numerous credentials including a master's in journalism, an
Edgar Allan Poe Award and a position as staff writer for the Los
Angeles Times? Are you considering a career in writing, but crave
advice from a professional?</p></p>

                            <p><p>The latest entry in its ongoing series of events, the Jewish
Studies Sunday Book and Discussion Group will be holding a
discussion on "Lost in Translation," a work by Eva Hoffman, on
Sunday, Jan. 22 on the third level of Hannon Library. This specific
event and the program as a whole are aimed to promote the
University's Jewish Studies Program and campus activities, to both
LMU students and denizens of the local community.</p></p>

                            <p><p>Dr. Kelly Younger is not only an English professor at Loyola
Marymount University but also an established playwright with work
staged around the world. On Wednesday, Jan. 18, he will share his
insights and lessons learned with the community along with short
performances of his original works with acting performed by LMU

                            Jewish Book Group takes a graphic look at ‘Genesis’  
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            Raeesah Reese, Staff Writer
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Posted: November 10, 2011
    </em></dd>
                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>The Jewish Sunday Book and Discussion Group will shake things up
with its conversation about a graphic novel called "The Book of
Genesis," by Robert Crumb. The group will hold its meeting on
Sunday, Nov. 13, and will discuss Crumb's visual presentation of
the first book of the Bible as well as the role of Jews in comic
books. The meeting will be led by Michael Brodsky, a professor of
art and art history.</p></p>

                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/laband-art-gallery-integrates-poetry-and-paintings-in-new-exhibit/article_ef62b32b-3355-5ee5-a4a5-d12f8be48299.html" title="Laband Art Gallery integrates poetry and paintings in new exhibit ">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/2/81/28168b6d-5bd4-57e6-a2c2-c26ed5b65f82/4e5d52f05b90a.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/laband-art-gallery-integrates-poetry-and-paintings-in-new-exhibit/article_ef62b32b-3355-5ee5-a4a5-d12f8be48299.html" title="Laband Art Gallery integrates poetry and paintings in new exhibit ">
                            Laband Art Gallery integrates poetry and paintings in new exhibit 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/laband-art-gallery-integrates-poetry-and-paintings-in-new-exhibit/article_ef62b32b-3355-5ee5-a4a5-d12f8be48299.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Amy Lee
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 2:15 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>The tragedy of Abu Ghraib detainees will be explored through the
integration of art and poetry at the exhibit of artist Daniel
Heyman’s artwork and reading by author and poet Nick Flynn, which
is taking place at the on-campus Laband Art Gallery tonight. The
event will start with a reading by Flynn from his memoir “The
Ticking is the Bomb” and poems from “Redacted,” a collection of
etchings and poetry in collaboration with Heyman. The event will
also feature a discussion with English professor Rubén Martinez. A
reception in honor of Flynn will follow with the opening of the
exhibition, “Bearing Witness: Daniel Heyman.”</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                            <p><p>The LMU Extension Program’s Spring Poetry Series kicks off its
season at 8 p.m. today in U-Hall 1857 with poets/authors Michael
Miller and Judith Pacht. The event is free and will start with
eight to 10 open readers and an introduction to upcoming writing
programs. This will be followed by readings from the two poets. The
audience will have the chance to talk to Miller and Pacht and also

                            Poetry to be a highlight at Pub Night 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/poetry-to-be-a-highlight-at-pub-night/article_78b21f48-5408-5e5e-870d-5cae04ae4b49.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">

                            <p><p>The fourth event of the <a href=
"http://libguides.lmu.edu/pubnight" target="_blank">“Pub Night”</a>
series will conclude its run for the fall semester with LMU
professors <a href=
"http://bellarmine.lmu.edu/english/faculty/wronsky.htm" target=
"_blank">Gail Wronsky</a> and <a href=
"http://www.lmu.edu/Page9228.aspx" target="_blank">Alicia
Partnoy</a> and world-renowned artist Gronk. At this Wednesday,
Dec. 8 event, the group will speak about Gronk’s book, “A Giant
Claw,” which was released in October. The presentation starts at
5:30 p.m. in the Von der Ahe suite in Hannon Library, and snacks
will be served.</p></p>

         <div class="day-partition">Monday 11/15/2010</div>
           
            

            <dl class="grid_  even-list-item">
    <dt class="bucket-photo">
                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-noir-continues-with-famed-author/article_dee8fa33-7436-5b97-83e2-0f97507203da.html" title="'L.A Noir' continues with famed author ">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/c/d9/cd9b0a13-68ec-53b9-8deb-c5ac43a0d910/4e5d3d53b2a5d.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-noir-continues-with-famed-author/article_dee8fa33-7436-5b97-83e2-0f97507203da.html" title="'L.A Noir' continues with famed author ">
                            'L.A Noir' continues with famed author 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-noir-continues-with-famed-author/article_dee8fa33-7436-5b97-83e2-0f97507203da.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Andrew Odeh
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:43 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>LMU, in its position atop the bluff, offers a panoramic view of
Los Angeles. Richard Rayner, this month’s presenting author for
Hannon Library’s “L.A. Noir” series, explores this panorama as a
means of newfound perspective on the city at large.  Rayner’s
nonfiction work, “A Bright and Guilty Place: Murder, Corruption,
and L.A.’s Scandalous Coming of Age,” presents a clear stance on
truthful noir within Los Angeles – the criminal drama and seedy
undertones, brimming with morality gone awry.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/b/4b/b4bb1f43-b090-5b55-a4f6-44ce85ba0c74/4e5d3ae41bfdc.preview-100.jpg" />

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-noir-continues-with-second-event/article_f7a5818c-081a-5dad-80ce-fd8c7281f259.html" title="‘L.A. Noir’ continues with second event ">
                            ‘L.A. Noir’ continues with second event 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-noir-continues-with-second-event/article_f7a5818c-081a-5dad-80ce-fd8c7281f259.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="2 images">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Kevin O'Keeffe
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:32 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>“Other cities have histories. Los Angeles has legends.” This is
the tagline for “L.A. Noir: The Struggle for the Soul of America’s
Most Seductive City,” a book by journalist and author <a href=
"http://www.johnbuntin.com/author.html" target="_blank">John
Buntin</a>. Tonight at the William H. Hannon Library, Buntin will
discuss his book as part of the library’s “L.A. Noir” event series.
In addition to Buntin, up-and-coming photography team Mitch Rouse
&amp; Brittany Jones will be speaking about their NOIR photography
project, a presentation that will work in conjunction with their
lecture to LMU professor Diane Meyer’s photography class today.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                            Pub Night features its first business speaker 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/pub-night-features-its-first-business-speaker/article_d2fec7aa-0f56-53ab-b568-ae828300dee5.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="2 images">

                            <p><p>It is the second year of Hannon Library’s existence on campus,
and it is also the second year of a few new library-organized event
series, including <a href="http://libguides.lmu.edu/pubnight"
target="_blank">Faculty Pub Night</a>. Though Pub Night is in its
sophomore year, on Wednesday the library will host its first
featured speaker who is from the College of Business
Administration.</p></p>

            <dl class="grid_  odd-list-item">
    <dt class="bucket-photo">
                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/noir-book-series-kicks-off-with-alum-author/article_b3302a63-35ae-5f21-b2d8-3b8885f99415.html" title="Noir book series kicks off with alum author ">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/2/99/29975f56-1114-5442-8a99-88823bbc2027/4e5d3d7f2e74e.preview-100.jpg" />

                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/noir-book-series-kicks-off-with-alum-author/article_b3302a63-35ae-5f21-b2d8-3b8885f99415.html" title="Noir book series kicks off with alum author ">
                            Noir book series kicks off with alum author 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/noir-book-series-kicks-off-with-alum-author/article_b3302a63-35ae-5f21-b2d8-3b8885f99415.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Emily Rome
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:43 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Starting next week, Hannon Library will provide the LMU
community with an opportunity to delve into the darkest and most
brooding of crime fiction with the new series, <a href=
"http://libguides.lmu.edu/content.php?pid=126838&amp;sid=1088676"
target="_blank">“The Dark Angel: Los Angeles Noir in Fact and
Fiction,”</a> also called “L.A. Noir.” LMU alumna and award-winning
author <a href="http://denisehamilton.com/" target="_blank">Denise
Hamilton</a> will speak at the first of five events in the series
when she comes to the library on Tuesday.</p></p>

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/homeboy-industries-founder-to-engage-discussion-on-campus/article_ed82d46a-7c6a-53e1-a7b6-a448a5de22cd.html" title="Homeboy Industries founder to engage discussion on campus ">
                            Homeboy Industries founder to engage discussion on campus 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/homeboy-industries-founder-to-engage-discussion-on-campus/article_ed82d46a-7c6a-53e1-a7b6-a448a5de22cd.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="2 images">

                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Kevin O'Keeffe
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:31 pm
    </em></dd>

                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Through the efforts of the William H. Hannon Library staff,
tomorrow evening the campus will host “A Conversation with Fr. Greg
Boyle.” It is the first in a yearlong series of talks and events
coordinated through Hannon Library. Fr. Gregory Boyle, S.J. will be
on campus to talk about his recently published book “Tattoos on the
Heart: The Power of Boundless Compassion” and his personal
experiences in his ministry.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/7/0d/70d99354-26fd-527d-ade0-d87b74fb9c27/4e5d3c8b05a86.preview-100.jpg" />

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/book-club-continues-monthly-discussions-of-jewish-novels/article_71f805a4-2757-5402-b875-03f255643324.html" title="Book club continues monthly discussions of Jewish novels ">
                            Book club continues monthly discussions of Jewish novels 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/book-club-continues-monthly-discussions-of-jewish-novels/article_71f805a4-2757-5402-b875-03f255643324.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Michelle Weiss
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:39 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>It has been four semesters since the <a href=
"http://libguides.lmu.edu/jewishbooks" target="_blank">Jewish Book
Club</a> was created, and now it is back for another year of group
discussions. On Sunday Sept. 12, the group will gather for the
first time this semester to discuss “The Five: A Novel of Jewish
Life in the Turn-of-the-Century Odessa,” by Vladimir Jabotinksy.
The novel closely mirrors the life of its author in an
autobiographical account of struggles with Jewish assimilation in
Russia as it follows the life of the middle- class Milgrom
family.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/4/47/447c684b-c643-5cab-ae3b-49b182598838/4e5d3ae46b309.preview-100.jpg" />

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/professors-introduce-extension-program-with-food-and-entertainment/article_7b72b097-f8b9-59fc-9d45-7a4de2eb9559.html" title="Professors introduce Extension Program with food and entertainment ">
                            Professors introduce Extension Program with food and entertainment 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/professors-introduce-extension-program-with-food-and-entertainment/article_7b72b097-f8b9-59fc-9d45-7a4de2eb9559.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Michelle Weiss
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:32 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Curious about the artistic talents of your professors? Tonight
you will have the chance to watch them perform in a casual and
informal setting during an event put on by the Extension program.
The <a href="http://www.lmu.edu/Page3539.aspx" target="_blank">LMU
Extension Program</a> is a place for adults in the community to be
educated by taking classes that interest them. Such classes include
writing, music, wine tasting and business courses. Not only does
the program strive to educate, but to also unify the community as a
whole.</p></p>

                            'Passion Magazine' expands and grows 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/passion-magazine-expands-and-grows/article_2062acb3-9fcb-59c6-ae62-d3a70b75ac4c.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">

                            <p><p>Just down the basement steps of the Sacred Heart Chapel lies a
cozy office equipped with a refrigerator, couch, Apple computers
and a meeting desk. With guides on the wall explaining the steps of
publishing and printing, the 'Passion Magazine' office has an
executive yet comfortable feel.'</p></p>

                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/6/46/64637f28-9fd5-5f0c-871b-415ecc49bc3b/4e5d38780bd30.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/get-spooked-by-short-stories/article_1d4e3052-9267-5f38-9f76-9614d3ec7d33.html" title="Get spooked by short stories ">
                            Get spooked by short stories 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/get-spooked-by-short-stories/article_1d4e3052-9267-5f38-9f76-9614d3ec7d33.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="5 images">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Emily Rome
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:22 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Feeling numb to the repetitive conventions of horror movies?
Still craving a good scare this Halloween? Conjure your creepy
voice, grab some candles (or flashlights if you're in campus
housing) and gather some friends for the reading of innovative
stories that will chill your bones.</p></p>

    <dt class="bucket-photo">
                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-times-festival-of-books-a-bookworm-s-heaven/article_7df8dee7-f110-5afe-bb2e-91aca6a0852c.html" title="L.A. Times Festival of Books: A bookworm's heaven ">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/0/86/0862b574-022d-56dc-b017-17751848bc38/4e5d38531ea51.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-times-festival-of-books-a-bookworm-s-heaven/article_7df8dee7-f110-5afe-bb2e-91aca6a0852c.html" title="L.A. Times Festival of Books: A bookworm's heaven ">
                            L.A. Times Festival of Books: A bookworm's heaven 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/l-a-times-festival-of-books-a-bookworm-s-heaven/article_7df8dee7-f110-5afe-bb2e-91aca6a0852c.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Erica Espejo
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:21 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>It was not a dark stormy night, but rather a bright and sunny
day. A familiar hungry caterpillar was illustrated on rows of
banners around the UCLA campus. This was where people of all ages
flocked to the Los Angeles Times Festival of Books this past
weekend. More than 100 authors of several literary genres - comics,
science fiction, children's, mystery, cooking and so much more -
attracted many local bibliophiles. Booksellers, publishers,
cultural organizations, university writing programs and food
vendors made up the hundreds of exhibitors on the UCLA campus. Book
fans could buy rare books, attend Q &amp; A sessions, autograph
signings and mingle with the many authors present at the festival.
With the exception of $9 for parking, the event was entirely free
of charge.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

    <dt class="bucket-photo">

                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/0/31/0310606f-e513-59a8-8cd6-f0654d848871/4e5d374d9c14d.preview-100.jpg" />

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/an-interview-with-audiobook-narrator-scott-brick/article_29b5b660-594f-5691-a90c-dcc06da6355a.html" title="An interview with audiobook narrator Scott Brick ">
                            An interview with audiobook narrator Scott Brick 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/an-interview-with-audiobook-narrator-scott-brick/article_29b5b660-594f-5691-a90c-dcc06da6355a.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">

                            By Nick Blodgett
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:17 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Scott Brick is a highly prolific, award winning, audiobook
narrator.' He has received over forty Earphone awards and been
featured in the pages of the Wall Street Journal. His recordings
span all genres, from mystery-such as Truman Capote's 'In Cold
Blood'-to science fiction-Philip K. Dick's 'Do Androids Dream of
Electric Sheep?'-and beyond. For more information on Scott and ways
in which to purchase his recordings go to <a href=
"http://www.scottbrickpresents.com">www.scottbrickpresents.com</a></p></p>

    <dt class="bucket-photo">
                                <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/short-stories-the-solution-for-busy-bookworms/article_77b46672-1925-5850-a9ec-bd460faca493.html" title="Short Stories: the solution for busy bookworms ">
                                    
                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/1/d5/1d5413c5-04cf-5c81-b9bf-502eb606269e/4e5d38d7b6dde.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/short-stories-the-solution-for-busy-bookworms/article_77b46672-1925-5850-a9ec-bd460faca493.html" title="Short Stories: the solution for busy bookworms ">
                            Short Stories: the solution for busy bookworms 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/short-stories-the-solution-for-busy-bookworms/article_77b46672-1925-5850-a9ec-bd460faca493.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Loyolan staff
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:24 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>For college students constantly trying to keep up with the
reading assignments of all our classes, the ironic dilemma is that
we don't have enough time to read. Read for pleasure, that is.
Alright, so some of our assigned reading is pleasurable, but rarely
is it as pleasurable as hunkering down in a comfy chair with a
novel of our own choosing. Those of us who once considered
ourselves avid readers when we were younger now feel undeserving of
the title because our list of completed pleasure books grows
smaller every year, while our list of 'to-read' books grows longer.
The busier we become, the more and more difficult it is to find
time to read a novel that we want to read.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/the-dirt-on-dirty-comic-books/article_dcf7559b-0728-5a7b-92aa-6289844db7b6.html" title="The dirt on dirty comic books ">
                            The dirt on dirty comic books 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/the-dirt-on-dirty-comic-books/article_dcf7559b-0728-5a7b-92aa-6289844db7b6.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>

                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Nick Blodgett
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">

            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>In a world where the First Amendment increasingly comes under
fire, whether it's vice presidential candidates trying to ban books
in a library or the recent high-profile obscenity cases of several
big names in the adult industry, one has all the more reason to
support those testing the waters of adult entertainment.</p></p>

                                        <img class="blox-img-loader" alt="" src="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/live/components/core_external_jquery_plugins/resources/images/place_holder.png?_dc=1375276585" data-original="http://bloximages.newyork1.vip.townnews.com/laloyolan.com/content/tncms/assets/v3/editorial/3/8c/38cb82ef-edff-566d-bede-c992cc7afd66/4e5d363dd1ce1.preview-100.jpg" />
                                    
                                </a>
                                
                            </dt>
                        
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/a-fan-s-guide-to-anime/article_1398ddfc-a5df-50ed-87d3-fab491c38e13.html" title="A fan's guide to anime ">
                            A fan's guide to anime 
                        </a>
                        
            <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/a-fan-s-guide-to-anime/article_1398ddfc-a5df-50ed-87d3-fab491c38e13.html" class="tn-tooltip" title="1 image">
            
            <span class="asset-related-icon image"></span>
        
            </a>
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Nick Blodgett
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:13 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Ever wondered what those funny characters with big eyes are all
about? Don't know what dojinshi is? Haven't a clue about cosplay?
You're in the right place, my friends. These and many more
astounding answers abound in this guide to the wild and wacky world
of Japanese animation. Obviously this article only scratches the
surface of anime. Its intention is to focus on the trickier
concepts for western fans to grasp.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

         <div class="day-partition">Monday 04/07/2008</div>
           
            

            <dl class="grid_  even-list-item">
    
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/wham-bang-pow/article_37ad660a-382a-5d2e-954c-17d1bedc2ca0.html" title="Wham! Bang! Pow! ">
                            Wham! Bang! Pow! 
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Nick Blodgett
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:12 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>I know as Americans we're supposed to hold some disdain for the
British; after all, there was that little revolution and there's
that whole thing of tea time in the afternoon, which, try as I
might, I can't get my head around. But credit must be given when
credit is due. Since the late 1970s the Brits have been putting out
the weekly comic anthology magazine, "2000 A.D.," featuring a wide
array of science fiction and fantasy, as well as a little horror
mixed in every now and again. Not only is "2000 A.D." worth
mentioning for the simple fact that it has been coming out weekly
for such a long time, it also boasts content that often goes above
and beyond the simple superhero fodder so popular in the United
States.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

         <div class="day-partition">Wednesday 03/19/2008</div>
           
            

            <dl class="grid_  odd-list-item">
    
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/robert-e-howard-in-comics/article_08e6a05f-30f1-5f63-bad2-7cc6d6ed674e.html" title="Robert E. Howard in Comics ">
                            Robert E. Howard in Comics 
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Nick Blodgett
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:14 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>Last week marked the loss of an iconic figure in the world of
fantasy-fiction and gaming. Gary Gygax, one of the co-creators of
the popular tabletop role-playing game, Dungeons and Dragons, died
at age 69. He, along with his cohorts, forever changed the way one
participates in a world of fantasy.</p></p>
                                    
                    
                
            
                <div class="clear"></div>
            </dd>

            <dl class="grid_  even-list-item">
    
                    
                    <dd class="bucket-headline">
                        <a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/spiderwick-is-fantastical/article_982c7568-4a8c-55fd-b085-4de4d794b3f2.html" title="Spiderwick is Fantastical ">
                            Spiderwick is Fantastical 
                        </a>
                        
                     </dd>
                    
                    <dd>
                        <p class="byline">
                            By Laurie Skaja
                        </p>
                    </dd>
                    
                    
    <dd>
    <em class="item-updated">
        Updated: August 30, 2011 - 12:09 pm
    </em></dd>

                    
            
            <dd>
                            


            
                <ul class="blox-flags">
                                  
                
                    <li></li>
                
                
                    <li></li>
                
                  </ul>
                

            
                
                      
                        
                            <p><p>"WARNING: Do not dare to read this book, for if you take one
fateful look, you face a deadly consequence." And do not dare to
read further if you would like to learn all of the secrets of The
Spiderwick Chronicles on your own.</p></p>

        <span class="blox-no-comments" >
        
            <span class="ui-icon ui-icon-comment blox-comments-icon"></span><a href="/arts_and_entertainment/literature/spiderwick-is-fantastical/article_982c7568-4a8c-55fd-b085-4de4d794b3f2.html?mode=comments">
